Close-up Macro photography Natural material Still life photography
Date: 2022-02-20 16:14:00
Caption: Happy #SlimeMoldSunday to Myxomycete lovers new and old! These amazing myxo fruiting bodies are Diachea leucopodia,¬†one of my favorites because of their¬†beautiful iridescence.¬† As with many slime molds, this species changes colors several times during its brief life cycle.¬† When they first arise from the white plasmodium, the fruiting bodies are white.¬† They then turn almost black, and as they mature and dry the peridium (outer covering of the spore-containing body) turns into these strikingly beautiful¬†iridescent blue, purple, and brown colors on a white stout stalk.¬† Although the individual¬†fruiting bodies are tiny, only 1-2mm tall, they can be easy to spot because they grow in dense and large clusters on leaves, grasses, and live and decaying plant material.¬† To see how tiny they are, see the second photo, which shows a few fruiting bodies on a twig with the tip of a fine point pen for scale. A little technical info for those of you who might be interested.¬† To photograph such tiny myxos with sharp detail, I use an extreme macro lens.¬† With such high magnifications, the depth of field (portion of the subject that is in sharp focus) is less than 0.05mm. To get a photo of the entire fruiting body in focus, I use a technique called focus stacking. My camera is mounted on a finely tuned rail, and the camera is moved in minuscule increments between each photo,¬†so that the focal point changes with each photo.¬† ¬†For this photo, I took 138 individual images, which were then ‚Äústacked‚Äù with specialized computer software that combines the most in-focus portions of each of the individual images into a composite image that shows everything in focus from front to back.

Fungus Polyporales Mushroom Close-up Trunk Medicinal mushroom Inonotus Natural material Macro photography Agaricomycetes
Date: 2022-08-02 05:09:43
Caption: Hexagonia tenuis fungi is plentiful in the regenerating native forests at the base of the escarpment. These areas were originally cleared for farmland and mining. The returning forests are only approximately 50 years into the process of establishing themselves again and I'm always in awe of their regenerative power. It's hard not to amorphosize natural phenomena with the constraints our language puts upon us. Fungi networks are described like the internet, beehives are described like officeworkers, but we know this is a crude way to narrate the complexity, abstraction, mystery and full expression of nature. So I tread tentatively knowing these words that follow are inept, but to experience a regenerating forest is to be part of a continual homecoming. With each species of native flora and fauna that returns I personally am exalted but there is no fanfare, fireworks or roll call within the forest itself. Instead a palatable gathering of strength and an emerging tranquillity spreads as each species reestablishes itself within the dynamics of the forest family. Many of the photos in this gallery are from this regenerating forest and it is a joy to share the homecoming of species like this fungi with you. #mycology #mycologysociety #fungus #mycologyphotography #fungilover #fungiphotography #fungifanatic #fantasticfungi #fungiofinstagram #fungiownunder #fungihunter #fungiaustralia #fungifreaks #fungihunting #fungiidentification #fungikingdom #fungilove #fungiphotography #fungioftheday #mushroom #mushrooms #mushlove #mushroomphotography #mushroomsofinstagram #australianfungi #fungi #forestbathing #forestfinds #naturesbeauty #forestlovers #biodiversity

Caption: You're so golden! üíõ The Golden-scruffy Collybia (Cyptotrama asprata) is found all around the world. In Australia it's primarily found along the east coast. With a cushion-shaped mushroom cap that grows up to 2.7 centimetres in diameter, it's covered in bright yellow and orange protrusions that lose their vibrancy as the mushroom ages. It's a saprobic fungus, so it processes dead and decaying wood from deciduous and coniferous trees. üå≤ üì∏ | Byteme via @inaturalistorg / Atlas of Living Australia *CSIRO does not endorse the consumption of any fungus referenced in #FungiFriday* #GoldenHour #OohSpiky #AtlasofLivingAustralia #WeLoveScience #CSIRO

Close-up Silver Macro photography Natural material Still life photography
Date: 2022-02-20 16:14:00
Caption: Happy #SlimeMoldSunday to Myxomycete lovers new and old! These amazing myxo fruiting bodies are Diachea leucopodia,¬†one of my favorites because of their¬†beautiful iridescence.¬† As with many slime molds, this species changes colors several times during its brief life cycle.¬† When they first arise from the white plasmodium, the fruiting bodies are white.¬† They then turn almost black, and as they mature and dry the peridium (outer covering of the spore-containing body) turns into these strikingly beautiful¬†iridescent blue, purple, and brown colors on a white stout stalk.¬† Although the individual¬†fruiting bodies are tiny, only 1-2mm tall, they can be easy to spot because they grow in dense and large clusters on leaves, grasses, and live and decaying plant material.¬† To see how tiny they are, see the second photo, which shows a few fruiting bodies on a twig with the tip of a fine point pen for scale. A little technical info for those of you who might be interested.¬† To photograph such tiny myxos with sharp detail, I use an extreme macro lens.¬† With such high magnifications, the depth of field (portion of the subject that is in sharp focus) is less than 0.05mm. To get a photo of the entire fruiting body in focus, I use a technique called focus stacking. My camera is mounted on a finely tuned rail, and the camera is moved in minuscule increments between each photo,¬†so that the focal point changes with each photo.¬† ¬†For this photo, I took 138 individual images, which were then ‚Äústacked‚Äù with specialized computer software that combines the most in-focus portions of each of the individual images into a composite image that shows everything in focus from front to back.

Date: 2022-10-03 11:47:28
Caption: Dendrocollybia racemosa - Branched shanklet Not my find but a collaborative effort to collect and record this rare species. I‚Äôm thrilled to get the opportunity to witness this one. The location has been recorded, and pending permissions, a sample will be making its way to Kew Gardens to be included in their genome sequencing projects and the national collection. Found by: Nicky Freeman Collected & record by: Iona Fraser @ashdownforage The species is characterised by its unusual stem, which is covered with short lateral branches. The branches often produce spherical slimeheads of translucent¬†conidiophores¬† on their swollen tips. The conidiophores produce conidia (asexual¬†spores) by¬†mitosis. Because the fungus can rely on either¬†sexual¬†or¬†asexual¬†modes of reproduction, fruit bodies sometimes have reduced or even missing caps. The unusual stems originate from black pea-sized structures called¬†sclerotia. The¬†anamorphic¬†form of the fungus, known as¬†Tilachlidiopsis¬†racemosa, is missing the sexual stage of its¬†life cycle. It can reproduce at relatively low temperatures, an adaptation believed to improve its ability to grow quickly and fruit on decomposing mushrooms. (Info via Wikimili) #allthingsfungi

Caption: These miniature white mushrooms are part of a large genus of small saprotrophic mushrooms called Mycena that are rarely more than a few centimeters in width. They are characterized by a white spore print, a small conical or bell-shaped cap, and a thin fragile stem. Most are gray or brown, but a few species have brighter colors.‚†Ä .‚†Ä Repost from @mycophoria üì∏ by: @corikindred ‚†Ä Check them both out for more fungal awesomeness.

Red Ingredient Fungus Mushroom Agaric Orange Close-up Macro photography Agaricaceae Medicinal mushroom Penny Bun Russula integra Mushroom
Date: 2022-02-06 08:49:48
Caption: Amanita muscaria, Fly Agaric, Amanitaceae. An introduced species to Australia, it is mycorrhizal with northern hemisphere conifers and hardwoods. Autumn and winter is when A. muscaria dominates the pine forests of Australia, though after the amount of rainfall we have had this summer, it‚Äôs not unusual to have them popping up now, in the same way Lactarius deliciosus (saffron milk cap) has been plentiful this summer. I was puzzled when I found this, as it was in the middle of a Eucalyptus forest, though after looking around I found two Pinus radiata growing a little way away. Known around the world for a variety of reasons, it has been portrayed in folklore, prepared in the kitchen for food, as medicine, and as a hallucinogen (it contains ibotenic acid, a neurotoxin which converts to muscimol, a psychoactive compound, once digested). Amanita muscaria poses a serious threat to the biodiversity of native fungi in the Myrtle Beech forests of Victoria and Tasmania, where it has formed Mycohrriza with Nothofagus cunninghamii.

Red Ingredient Fungus Mushroom Agaric Orange Close-up Macro photography Agaricaceae Medicinal mushroom Penny Bun Russula integra Mushroom
Date: 2022-02-06 08:49:48
Caption: Amanita muscaria, Fly Agaric, Amanitaceae. An introduced species to Australia, it is mycorrhizal with northern hemisphere conifers and hardwoods. Autumn and winter is when A. muscaria dominates the pine forests of Australia, though after the amount of rainfall we have had this summer, it‚Äôs not unusual to have them popping up now, in the same way Lactarius deliciosus (saffron milk cap) has been plentiful this summer. I was puzzled when I found this, as it was in the middle of a Eucalyptus forest, though after looking around I found two Pinus radiata growing a little way away. Known around the world for a variety of reasons, it has been portrayed in folklore, prepared in the kitchen for food, as medicine, and as a hallucinogen (it contains ibotenic acid, a neurotoxin which converts to muscimol, a psychoactive compound, once digested). Amanita muscaria poses a serious threat to the biodiversity of native fungi in the Myrtle Beech forests of Victoria and Tasmania, where it has formed Mycohrriza with Nothofagus cunninghamii.

Date: 2022-08-02 05:09:43
Caption: Hexagonia tenuis fungi is plentiful in the regenerating native forests at the base of the escarpment. These areas were originally cleared for farmland and mining. The returning forests are only approximately 50 years into the process of establishing themselves again and I'm always in awe of their regenerative power. It's hard not to amorphosize natural phenomena with the constraints our language puts upon us. Fungi networks are described like the internet, beehives are described like officeworkers, but we know this is a crude way to narrate the complexity, abstraction, mystery and full expression of nature. So I tread tentatively knowing these words that follow are inept, but to experience a regenerating forest is to be part of a continual homecoming. With each species of native flora and fauna that returns I personally am exalted but there is no fanfare, fireworks or roll call within the forest itself. Instead a palatable gathering of strength and an emerging tranquillity spreads as each species reestablishes itself within the dynamics of the forest family. Many of the photos in this gallery are from this regenerating forest and it is a joy to share the homecoming of species like this fungi with you. #mycology #mycologysociety #fungus #mycologyphotography #fungilover #fungiphotography #fungifanatic #fantasticfungi #fungiofinstagram #fungiownunder #fungihunter #fungiaustralia #fungifreaks #fungihunting #fungiidentification #fungikingdom #fungilove #fungiphotography #fungioftheday #mushroom #mushrooms #mushlove #mushroomphotography #mushroomsofinstagram #australianfungi #fungi #forestbathing #forestfinds #naturesbeauty #forestlovers #biodiversity

Water is also a challenge here, all of our waters are invested with parasites like E.Coli, Giardia and many more unwanted visitors. We are blessed enough to be able to properly filter our water, not all of our local neighbors have this ability. It is in this spirit that we, feel so passionate about water quality in our home of Lake Atitlan, Guatemala. Date: 2022-10-03 11:47:28
Caption: Dendrocollybia racemosa - Branched shanklet Not my find but a collaborative effort to collect and record this rare species. I‚Äôm thrilled to get the opportunity to witness this one. The location has been recorded, and pending permissions, a sample will be making its way to Kew Gardens to be included in their genome sequencing projects and the national collection. Found by: Nicky Freeman Collected & record by: Iona Fraser @ashdownforage The species is characterised by its unusual stem, which is covered with short lateral branches. The branches often produce spherical slimeheads of translucent¬†conidiophores¬† on their swollen tips. The conidiophores produce conidia (asexual¬†spores) by¬†mitosis. Because the fungus can rely on either¬†sexual¬†or¬†asexual¬†modes of reproduction, fruit bodies sometimes have reduced or even missing caps. The unusual stems originate from black pea-sized structures called¬†sclerotia. The¬†anamorphic¬†form of the fungus, known as¬†Tilachlidiopsis¬†racemosa, is missing the sexual stage of its¬†life cycle. It can reproduce at relatively low temperatures, an adaptation believed to improve its ability to grow quickly and fruit on decomposing mushrooms. (Info via Wikimili) #allthingsfungi

Yellow Orange Fungus Macro photography Mushroom
Date: 2024-05-26 11:18:21
Caption: Growing a new fungus is always interesting. This is Cordyceps militaris #cordycepsmilitaris a fungi that until recently was not allowed to be grown here in Australia. Now we can legally grow this, I was curious to give it a go - especially after investing so much time into trying to grow Cordyceps gunnii, unsuccessfully! Not my best grow! And I have been watching lots of US growers really get to dial these in to be an art. But I grew these on white rice with no nutrients to start out so I could get an idea of growth, yield, and other characteristics that may help later! One big hint, don't try to grow these when it is hot without cooling! #guerrillamycology #fungiculture #üçÑ #fungi #fungus #funghi #hongos #myceliumrunning #radicalmycology #radmycology #thinkfungi #mycology #mycophile #mycophilia #mycelium #mushrooms #myceliumrunning #myceliumnetwork #myceliummood #cordyceps #cordycepsmilitaris #cordycepsgunnii #introducedfungi #notnativefungi #notwildfungi #ethnomycology #entheogenicfungi #fungiphotography #mushroomphotography

Date: 2024-05-26 11:18:21
Caption: Growing a new fungus is always interesting. This is Cordyceps militaris #cordycepsmilitaris a fungi that until recently was not allowed to be grown here in Australia. Now we can legally grow this, I was curious to give it a go - especially after investing so much time into trying to grow Cordyceps gunnii, unsuccessfully! Not my best grow! And I have been watching lots of US growers really get to dial these in to be an art. But I grew these on white rice with no nutrients to start out so I could get an idea of growth, yield, and other characteristics that may help later! One big hint, don't try to grow these when it is hot without cooling! #guerrillamycology #fungiculture #üçÑ #fungi #fungus #funghi #hongos #myceliumrunning #radicalmycology #radmycology #thinkfungi #mycology #mycophile #mycophilia #mycelium #mushrooms #myceliumrunning #myceliumnetwork #myceliummood #cordyceps #cordycepsmilitaris #cordycepsgunnii #introducedfungi #notnativefungi #notwildfungi #ethnomycology #entheogenicfungi #fungiphotography #mushroomphotography

Date: 2022-05-23 10:17:27
Caption: BLUE OR GREEN OR SOMETHING IN BETWEEN? . Not all fungi has stems and gills. This Ascomycetes variety is known as Chlorociboria aeruginascens, and comes in amazingly vibrant colours. One thing I love about it, is that it can stain the wood it grows on, filling the forest with tiny smurf logs. . These lil discs are about 3-4mm across. But what colour would you say these are? . Nikon D780 Sigma 105mm f2.8 Macro . . . . #tasmania #mycology #mushrooms #mushroomphotography #macrophotography #macromushroom #fungiphotography #fungi #fungihunter #ascomycetes #mynikonlife #sigmaphotoaustralia

Green Macro photography
Date: 2022-05-30 10:39:07
Caption: TRACK-SIDE TREATS . Lately I've been venturing off track in search of new specimens and species. But last Friday I had to be slightly less* intrepid as I was accompanied by my lovely wife, on a stroll of the waterfall circuit of Mount Field National Park. . Turns out I didn't need to enter the lair of the leeches, as this gorgeous Chlorociboria aeruginascens cluster was conveniently positioned right on the side of the track. Jackpot! . Love these blue green gems. A week or so ago I posted a snap of these and the concensus was that they were emerald or jade in colour (among other suggestions). I haven't played with the colour of these at all, and this time I'm seeing much more blue in the caps. Nature amirite? . *we did go off track once to explore the second tier of Russell Falls. Fun times. .
